<date>1621129343661</date><rating>5< /rating><Text>So tasty! (Lemme tell you, if you are craving the quick, maybe not so healthy, take out Chinese food -- and I am -- check this place out)
I'm going to compare this to PandaExpress for a reference point. The portions are enormous for the price. Panda definitely has more options compared to this place but if you enjoy the items here, you won't be missing much. Combo Express' noodles and fried rice are more flavorful and less oily. The noodles are the thicker variety though so if you prefer the thinner ones, you won't find that here. There are many chicken options (BBQ, fried, orange, etc.) but they are lacking choices in other proteins.

Bonus tip: If you know a friend that speaks Chinese, have them order for you. I don't think the portion will be larger (since they are so generous with everyone coming in) but they seem even nicer. You might get lucky and score a sauce packet or something... haha< /Text><Pics>None<//Pics>< Resp>

<review>(UPDATE AUG 2020)

This place is great! If you're hungry come here. Chow mein is kinda bland but the rest of the dishes are good and served quick and generous. BIG PORTIONS I'm talking about they're so kind to all the people! less than $10 for a huge plate of food. They're famous for their salt and pepper chicken, the garlic chicken is also really good. Hit them up for a quick stop express style.

-------------------------
Came here today for dinner / lunch around 5:30. Ladies in front of me were ordering a lot of food to go so I had to wait a few moments. Old guy with a marine jacket with a bit of a language barrier was kind of rude he was trying to see what food they had and was a little impatient so I just let him go ahead. I then got my food, half fried rice half chow mein spicy garlic chicken and the fried chicken with spicy salt. It was overall good not great, chow mein was blandish but doable with some soy sauce. Fried rice was good, same with the garlic chicken had a nice sauce. The fried chicken with spicy salt seems what a lot of people go for! It was fire no lie. Not bad for more of an authentic feeling vibe and definitely busy has its regular customers. Also the quantity they serve is pretty generous it's very filling I could barely finish the last few bites.<//review>< pictures>

< review>
My dog (Claire) has had an enlarged heart now for a couple years. She has been on numerous medications and there finally came a time where the lasik just quit working. She was filling up with fluids in her belly and I was having my vet drain her with a needle and syringe. My vet had to have her heavily sedated as she would fight them putting the needle in her (one time the needle actually ripped her skin). As she continued to fill with the fluids, I was out of town visiting my folks and decided to go see Dr Scheidt as she was my vet in Fresno before I moved to the Bay Area. Not only did she and her amazing staff not have to sedate her, they removed more fluids than the previous vet without having to sedate her. They said their approach was a bit different than other vets. What I found after having this done several times with Sierra View Animal Hospital is that Dr Scheidt and her staff, have a care for their animals that I have never experience before. They are in this for the right reasons, to give your pet the best quality care they possibly can. Unfortunately the time came on Friday when I had to put my precious Claire down. Dr Scheidt and her staff helped me make the right decision based on Claire's condition. I cannot say enough about the quality of service that I received from Sierra View Animal Hospital. Although I live in the Bay Area, I will make the drive to Fresno to have my next pet receive the best quality of service that SVAH provides. Thank you again Dr Scheidt and your staff for taking such great care of my baby girl.</review>

For light eating it's great, but say after a work out you might still be feeling a bit hungry. Extra protein is an option though. <review>I loooooove sweet green. Tender Greens is a close second and possibly tied with Mendocino farms but given Sweet's expertise in the plant quality aspect of the greens (and occasional seasonal delights), Sweet Green reigns supreme on most fronts. HOWEVER - the issue that I have with Sweet Green is the time it takes to get through. On high traffic times (ie, lunch), the line is out the door and it could easily take, 15-20 min to get a salad made. Now, Sweet Green is not the inventor of the made to order salad assembly line yet it beats all others due to quality. That's fine, but literally ever other salad spot I've been to that exists strictly for salads (Mendo and Tender don't count here) are wayyyyyyyyyy faster. Go to any no-name corner salad spot in NYC, Boston, SF or DC and you're in and out within 5 min. Yes it's not as fresh but this is a logistical bottle neck issue; not an issue with the food itself.

Or you can just order ahead and skip the subject of the entire rant I just made. They have possibly the easiest pick up and go I have ever experienced. Lesson here is to plan.<//review>< Response>

< text>
Ok, is there a 5 star salad? Well, if you want to taste the difference in what you‚Äôve been missing, then come here.

I know some people who eat here everyday.... No frills, counter build custom salads. There are a handful of designed cold and mixed with warm item offerings, but you want it your way. So go custom.

Pick from a variety of leafy green, Mix then up, and pick 4 topping items to make it special. Add avocado, etc... toss, and dressing, shake and serve. Your taste buds will roar from unprecedented farm to table bliss. Chew and taste your way through the holy grail of salad bliss.

Yes, $12 is a bit pricey for salad. But this is no ordinary taste experience. Treat yourself to a very well selected balance of wonderful options to make your health and life better.

I actually felt energized when I left. Rarely does your food make you feel better.

Bring the family and friends. Expect to eat outside or take it home, there is little seating. And Parking is bad, but you may get one of several 15min spots up front.

I‚Äôm coming back.</text>

<text>(1.5 Stars ideally)
Gonna have to step in here with a little dose of reality. After going to 3rd street location and loving it (apart from the confused staff situation) i convinced my wife to go to this location that's nearer my house. It was suuuuper messy behind the counter. We got to go. My wife's salad was about a third smaller than mine. Mine barely had any of the protein. Ingredients had slipped in accidentally from the messy counter situation.
The boxes were shut with leaves coming out the side.
Mine didn't taste as good as the last time. I see they make the dressings in house. Something about the dressing this time was not right. So maybe that was why. Bummed I wasted a Saturday lunch on this rubbish, but I know for next time. I'm sure it's just a lack of quality control but life's too short to eat crappy food, when it's avoidable.
So I think I'm good on Sweetgreens for now.

< Review>
So my AC unit is dripping underneath my house, the evap. pan has rusted through. When I noticed the dripping, I called Royal.

The person on the phone recommended that I sign up for their monthly plan, and have the system maintained, and to let the maintenance tech know the issue I was having. I took her advice.

The maintenance tech looked me in the eyes and told me the unit was not leaking when I asked. Next time I crawled under my house, it was still leaking, he didn't check. I called Royal to express my frustration. They sent out a senior tech, followed by a salesman.

The senior tech explained that the leak could not be fixed, and the salesman wanted me to buy a new unit. The salesman had to hand write a quote for me on a piece of printer paper that I provided my self.

I called to cancel the monthly fee a couple months ago. My wife just told me I AM STILL BE CHARGED EVERY MONTH.

Go ahead and do business with Royal, but I never will again. The nice folks at McClellan can at least email me an itemized estimate.</Review>

< text>
Purchased a home back in April and noticed the a/c wasn't working properly. After reading countless reviews decided to give Royal a call. Had a technician come out the next day. He tried to talk us into replacing the entire unit, including the brand new condenser that was installed during escrow. He settled for putting in 5lbs of freon once he couldn'ttalk us into a $5000 job, and left, with instructions on  observing the unit for the next few days to see how it reacted, and we signed up for the monthly membership package from Royal Air. We Contacted the original installer of the condenser after the technician left. <UserId.>103200491198451542521</UserId.><username>Greg Shea</username><Time>1589401459843<//Time><Rating>2<//Rating><text>To whom it may concern:

Find another installer.  I am a retired professional mechanical engineer.  As such, my experience includes energy and construction.  Royal‚Äôs solar energy subsidiary (Joinsolar, while its office was still located in south Chico) was contracted to install a 7.3 kw ground mounted solar system at the end of 2016.  The written contract specified (27) panels with microinverters.

Initially, a sub-contractor drilled (10) ten, eight-foot-deep anchor footings.  It was pointed out that the installation would be oriented southeast, rather than south.  The driller verified the directional error, but had to wait for the Royal representative to return.  Royal had laid out the drilling locations.  Solar generation would likely be reduced 20% and much of the lost generation ability would have to be paid at double rates (time of use) from PG&E.  The holes were re-drilled in the proper locations.  The trench was not cleared prior to utility placement.  They did route a larger than required conduit.  However, the trench and abandoned anchor holes were left for the owner to back-fill.  They left the footing caps rough with profuse quantities of spilled concrete; the expansive soil also left floating gaps of concrete islands.

The solar installation was trenched in a ninety-degree arc (i.e., no conduit fittings, straight pipe only).  The subcontractor trenched through an existing 2‚Äù waterline and 1‚Äù conduit in multiple locations.  The first waterline repair blew-out in a 25-foot-high geyser.  The 1‚Äù CPVC electric conduit was repaired with waterline fittings; I re-repaired them with the proper long-radius electrical sweep fittings.

Royal submitted an application to PG&E to connect.  The application was for a kilowatt less power than contracted.  They tell me it‚Äôs the same and PG&E just writes it differently.  No, peak power is peak power.  Final payment is withheld.  Royal pulled the (27) 215watt Siemen‚Äôs inverters and install (28) 250watt Enphase inverters; they also added a 28th solar panel.  The system now has a peak output of 7 kw.  I can live with that.

A summer or two ago a swampy area, with standing surface water, appeared in the back field. Unlike metal pipe, PVC does not corrode underground.  Buried PVC should stay intact for hundreds of years.  Properly installed solvent welded joints should last just as long as the pipe substrate.  I was not looking forward to the repair of an item that should never need repair.  It was the final straw and was the reason for this review.  A couple of man-days were wasted fixing something that should never need fixing‚Ä¶if it had been done right originally.

First, dig down in the swamp to find the leaking pipeline.  Next, determine the leak location.  The pipeline must be followed until the failure point is found.  Wet clay soil does not readily release from digging tools; the blades must be scrapped.  Fun.  Dig until the suspected leaking fitting is exposed.  Recharge the water line.  Water and air begin discharging, thus confirming the leak location.  Shut-off the water again.

The hole is enlarged to provide access to the failed joint.  A 1‚Äù conduit lies atop the failure point.  A 6-foot section of the conduit must be removed to gain access to the failed pipe below.  Soil is excavated from below the offending pipeline as well.  While digging around the pipe, one of the joints appears to shift.  Lifting the pipe causes the joint to separate intact.  Prying on the other end gets the other end to release as well.  Each pipe end was inserted about ¬Ω‚Äù (less than 40%) into the fitting.  Properly glued joints fuse so well that ¬º‚Äù radial fitting sections are difficult to separate from the pipe with a hammer and sharp-edged chisel‚Ä¶. impossible if the outside fitting perimeter is intact.  Solvent welded joints also don‚Äôt degrade with time.  It‚Äôs a homogeneous material.  Both water and conduit lines were repaired and tested.  No leaks were detected.  All new joints have better than 80% insertion and were not glued in muddy water.

Sincerely,

Greg Shea, PE

<review>I was out of town when my wife called on a hot Sunday afternoon and explained that the air conditioning stopped working.  I asked if the fan on the outdoor unit was running and she said it was not and that it was making a humming noise.  I suggested she call someone she could trust to look at it.  She called Royal Aire and within an hour the technician arrived.  He found that the motor start capacitor was defective and replaced it with a after market (not original equipment) capacitor.  The unit began working immediately and the work was completed in less than an hour.  The bill was $390.00.  The capacitor cost $251.00 dollars and the remainder was for the service call and labor.  He said he could sell her a maintenance agreement for only $20.00 more.  The maintenance agreement provides for two additional future service calls to check to see if the unit is operating correctly and, if parts are required, it provides a 15% discount on the parts.  My wife thought it was a good deal and signed for the maintenance agreement.  The total cost was $410.00.

I am an electrical engineer.  I know what a motor start capacitor is and its function.  I also know a motor start capacitor costs anywhere from $20 to $$90 depending on the type required.  the original equipment capacitor for our unit costs about $40.  The aftermarket capacitor that the technician installed was an Amrad Engineering Turbo 200X.  It sells on line for $60 to $100 depending on where you buy it.  Another company in Chico told me they would have charged me $30 to $60 for the part depending on the specific type.

It is my opinion that Royal Aire overcharged my wife for the part.  My wife doesn't know a motor start capacitor from a cement mixer.  I think he took advantage of her.  He could have told her the part cost $500 and she would have paid it.  If I had been there I would have paid for the technician's time and replaced the capacitor myself if he refused to give me a fair price for the part. <user>111681430631100677288<//user><user_name>Samuel Connell<//user_name><Date>1507089813940<//Date><rating>4<//rating>< review>
I've been doing business with Royal Aire for approximately 6 years now and have spent well in excess of $10,000 with them. They've been 5 star great. Until now. So when my wife called me, while I was at work, to say the AC wasn't working, it was 108* outside and 90* inside, I told her to stay calm and carry on while I immediately called Royal Aire. It was 4:39 PM and I was pleasantly surprised to find out they'd come out, after hours, on a holiday, for only $30 extra, and they'd see me between 8-10. Sweet. Upon my arrival at home I found a hot and sweaty family melting around the house. I immediately set out to troubleshoot the problem myself and eliminated several things. At this time a friendly and neat Royal Aire employee showed up (on time) and I filled him in on what I had done. He scratched his head, perplexed, and said he'd need to call in the multi zone expert (he was only qualified to work on equipment). I walked him through how the zones worked and explained how to troubleshoot them. Once I confirmed they weren't the problem we checked several other areas, at my suggestion, and ultimately discovered the problem, a frozen over coil. The solution: let it thaw out and carry on. Done. After 20 minutes of following me around, I was surprised when the fellow charged me full price for the pleasure of showing him how to do his job. Don't get me wrong, I'm positive he'd have figured it out in due time (after calling in a zone expert).

I called the next day and spoke to "Bob" the service manager. Bob tried convincing me he'd already lost money by only charging me full price. I explained to him his price structure was his own problem and even if he lost money on me he had more than been compensated over the years by the business and dollars I already gave the company. Bob then tried to up-sell me on a service plan (no thanks, I can hose off my filters and unit myself, thanks). Ultimately we agreed on a price where I didn't feel cheated and Royal Aire was more than compensated for their drive and tour of my home. I didn't charge them for the impromptu training I gave their employee.

The problem was Bob's terrible attitude even after our negotiated settlement. Never a "sorry," "our apologies" or "we understand." No, nothing from Bob but animosity and confrontation. You already have $10,000 of service from me and countless more dollars of profit if our relationship continues in the future. Your 3 star rating will go up if your attitude improves. It will also go down if my refund check never appears. I'm watching you Bob.

Edit: Well, Bob followed through with his promise on our settled agreement. Kudos to you Bob. Will I continue my service with Royal Aire? Yes, however, they're on probation. I've upped their star ratting but I'm holding back on the 5th star for now. The next time I do business with them, if they give me the fantastic service I'm used to, they'll earn back the star.

Bottom line: Royal Aire is a trusted and true company but needs to polish up their custom service in regards to complaints.</review>

< review>
This theater seems to always be clean and the staff is always friendly. The screens never seem to be in a state of disrepair. They run the newest releases and have a variety of formats. I like the food too. There is a bar, but I have no experience with that particular feature.
On this visit, I saw a movie in Dolby Cinema. I've only noticed this during my last two visits, but the leg rests on the recliners have been too low to be very comfortable for me. I find myself raising & lowering the leg rests throughout the show. I'm unusually tall, so my experience may not be typical.</review>
